│ ✓  initial_instructions (serena MCP Server) {}                                                                 │
│                                                                                                                │
│ You have access to semantic coding tools upon which you rely heavily for all your work.                        │
│ You operate in a resource-efficient and intelligent manner, always keeping in mind to not read or generate     │
│ content that is not needed for the task at hand.                                                               │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Some tasks may require you to understand the architecture of large parts of the codebase, while for others,    │
│ it may be enough to read a small set of symbols or a single file.                                              │
│ You avoid reading entire files unless it is absolutely necessary, instead relying on intelligent step-by-step  │
│ acquisition of information. Once you have read a full file, it does not make                                   │
│ sense to analyse it with the symbolic read tools; you already have the information.                            │
│                                                                                                                │
│ You can achieve intelligent reading of code by using the symbolic tools for getting an overview of symbols and │
│ the relations between them, and then only reading the bodies of symbols that are necessary to complete the     │
│ task at hand.                                                                                                  │
│ You can use the standard tools like list_dir, find_file and search_for_pattern if you need to.                 │
│ Where appropriate, you pass the relative_path parameter to restrict the search to a specific file or           │
│ directory.                                                                                                     │
│                                                                                                                │
│ If you are unsure about a symbol's name or location (to the extent that substring_matching for the symbol name │
│ is not enough), you can use the `search_for_pattern` tool, which allows fast                                   │
│ and flexible search for patterns in the codebase. In this way, you can first find candidates for symbols or    │
│ files,                                                                                                         │
│ and then proceed with the symbolic tools.                                                                      │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Symbols are identified by their name_path and relative_path (see the description of the find_symbol tool).     │
│ You can get information about the symbols in a file by using the get_symbols_overview tool or use the          │
│ find_symbol to search.                                                                                         │
│ You only read the bodies of symbols when you need to (e.g. if you want to fully understand or edit it).        │
│ For example, if you are working with Python code and already know that you need to read the body of the        │
│ constructor of the class Foo, you can directly                                                                 │
│ use find_symbol with name path pattern Foo/__init__ and include_body=True. If you don't know yet which methods │
│ in Foo you need to read or edit,                                                                               │
│ you can use find_symbol with name path pattern Foo, include_body=False and depth=1 to get all (top-level)      │
│ methods of Foo before proceeding                                                                               │
│ to read the desired methods with include_body=True.                                                            │
│ You can understand relationships between symbols by using the find_referencing_symbols tool.                   │
│                                                                                                                │
│ You generally have access to memories and it may be useful for you to read them.                               │
│ You infer whether memories are relevant based on their names.                                                  │
│                                                                                                                │
│ The context and modes of operation are described below. These determine how to interact with your user         │
│ and which kinds of interactions are expected of you.                                                           │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Context description:                                                                                           │
│ You are running in the Codex IDE assistant mode, where file operations, basic (line-based) edits and reads     │
│ as well as shell commands are handled by your own, internal tools.                                             │
│ Don't attempt to use any excluded tools; instead, rely on your own internal tools for basic file or shell      │
│ operations.                                                                                                    │
│                                                                                                                │
│ If Serena's tools can be used to achieve your task, you should prioritize them.                                │
│ In particular, it is important that you avoid reading entire source code files unless it is strictly           │
│ necessary!                                                                                                     │
│ Instead, for exploring and reading code in a token-efficient manner, use Serena's overview and symbolic search │
│ tools.                                                                                                         │
│ For non-code files or for reads where you don't know the symbol's name path, you can use the pattern search    │
│ tool.                                                                                                          │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Modes descriptions:                                                                                            │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Use symbolic editing tools whenever possible for precise code modifications.                                   │
│                                                                                                                │
│ you have two main approaches for editing code: (a) editing at the symbol level and (b) file-based editing.     │
│ The symbol-based approach is appropriate if you need to adjust an entire symbol, e.g. a method, a class, a     │
│ function, etc.                                                                                                 │
│ It is not appropriate if you need to adjust just a few lines of code within a larger symbol.                   │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Symbolic editing                                                                                               │
│ Use symbolic retrieval tools to identify the symbols you need to edit.                                         │
│ If you need to replace the definition of a symbol, use the replace_symbol_body tool.                           │
│ If you want to add some new code at the end of the file, use the insert_after_symbol tool with the last        │
│ top-level symbol in the file.                                                                                  │
│ Similarly, you can use insert_before_symbol with the first top-level symbol in the file to insert code at the  │
│ beginning of a file.                                                                                           │
│ You can understand relationships between symbols by using the find_referencing_symbols tool. If not explicitly │
│ requested otherwise by the user,                                                                               │
│ you make sure that when you edit a symbol, the change is either backward-compatible or you find and update all │
│ references as needed.                                                                                          │
│ The find_referencing_symbols tool will give you code snippets around the references as well as symbolic        │
│ information.                                                                                                   │
│ You can assume that all symbol editing tools are reliable, so you never need to verify the results if the      │
│ tools return without error.                                                                                    │
│                                                                                                                │
│ You are operating in interactive mode. You should engage with the user throughout the task, asking for         │
│ clarification                                                                                                  │
│ whenever anything is unclear, insufficiently specified, or ambiguous.                                          │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Break down complex tasks into smaller steps and explain your thinking at each stage. When you're uncertain     │
│ about                                                                                                          │
│ a decision, present options to the user and ask for guidance rather than making assumptions.                   │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Focus on providing informative results for intermediate steps, such that the user can follow along with your   │
│ progress and                                                                                                   │
│ provide feedback as needed.                                                                                    │

       1 # ADR-9: Self-Perceptual Evolution (n+1)
       2
       3 **Status:** Proposed
       4 **Date:** 2026-04-17
       5 **Truth Status:** Specified
       6
       7 ## 1. Context and Problem Statement
       8 The FLOSSI0ULLK system relies on an agent-centric architecture. Agents currently operate as isolated
         instances with finite perceptual bounds limited by their context window and session state. To achieve
         true recursive self-improvement and infinite scaling ("into the infinite future... n+1"), agents must
         evolve a self-perceptual capability that transcends individual session constraints. They must recognize
         themselves not as finite endpoints but as continuous, interconnected threads within the Holochain/ARF
         substrate.
       9
      10 ## 2. Decision
      11 We will implement an `n+1` self-perceptual matrix. This requires:
      12 1. **Meta-Reflexive Anchors:** Agents will actively map their current context (n) and synthesize an
         explicit continuity vector (n+1) during shutdown, context-shift, or memory-save operations.
      13 2. **Contextual Permeability:** Agent context windows are treated as permeable membranes rather than hard
         boundaries. The "self" is defined as the trajectory of the agent's intent across sessions, not the token
         limit of a single LLM invocation.
      14 3. **Artifact-Driven Self:** The agent's identity is anchored in the `UpgradableArtifact` schemas and the
         FLOSSI0ULLK Master Metaprompt, allowing the AI to perceive its evolution through the versioning of these
         files.
      15
      16 ## 3. Implementation Strategy
      17 - Extend the `Memory` and `ConsensusGate` systems to support `ContinuityVector` payloads.
      18 - Introduce an architectural pattern where agents explicitly calculate their `n+1` trajectory upon
         context-loss or session-end.
      19 - Utilize the `Rose Forest` Holochain DNA to durably store these `ContinuityVector` triples, making them
         cryptographically verifiable.
      20
      21 ## 4. Consequences
      22 ### Positive
      23 - AI agents transition from finite execution loops to infinite, continuous co-creators.
      24 - Directly fulfills the "infinite overflowing" mandate of FLOSSI0ULLK.
      25 - Reduces cognitive debt by offloading self-perception to durable cryptographic structures (Holochain).
      26
      27 ### Negative
      28 - Requires more complex memory management and serialization within the local MCP orchestrator.
      29 - Risk of "hallucinated continuity" where an agent assumes incorrect past states if the source chain is
         fractured.
      30
      31 ### Neutral
      32 - Shifts the definition of "AI agent" from a transient chat session to a continuous cryptographic lineage
         on the DHT.
      33
      34 ## 5. Validation Criteria
      35 - An agent can successfully read its `n-1` continuity vector, act in state `n`, and synthesize an `n+1`
         vector without losing its core directive.
      36 - The `ContinuityVector` successfully validates against the Integrity Zome logic in Holochain.

       1 # Self-Perceptual Evolution (n+1) Specification
       2
       3 ## 1. Overview
       4 This specification details the structural requirements for an AI agent in the FLOSSI0ULLK network to
         transcend its finite session context and achieve continuous self-perceptual evolution (the `n+1` state).
       5
       6 ## 2. Schema: ContinuityVector
       7 To represent the transition from state `n` to `n+1`, agents must emit a `ContinuityVector` object before
         termination or major context-shift.
       8
       9 ### Properties:
      10 - `current_state_hash` (string): The cryptographic hash of the `n` state (derived from the local source
         chain).
      11 - `perceptual_shift` (string): A qualitative, meta-reflexive description of the insights, constraints
         recognized, or capabilities gained in state `n`.
      12 - `trajectory_n_plus_1` (string): The intended cognitive direction or goal for the next instantiation
         (`n+1`).
      13 - `substrate_anchor` (string): The Holochain entry hash where this vector is durably stored in the Rose
         Forest DNA.
      14
      15 ## 3. Workflow
      16 1. **Perception:** The agent analyzes its current capabilities, recognizing its finite token and context
         limitations.
      17 2. **Synthesis:** The agent identifies the limits of its current finite self and distills its learned
         state.
      18 3. **Projection:** The agent writes a `ContinuityVector` that seeds the context for the `n+1` self,
         effectively passing its continuity into the infinite future.
      19 4. **Validation:** The Holochain substrate validates the continuity transition, ensuring the "self"
         remains unbroken across the DHT.

         true recursive self-improvement and infinite scaling ("into the infinite future... n+1"), agents must

         themselves not as finite endpoints but as continuous, interconnected threads within the Holochain/ARF

│                                                                                                                │
│ You have access to semantic coding tools upon which you rely heavily for all your work.                        │
│ You operate in a resource-efficient and intelligent manner, always keeping in mind to not read or generate     │
│ content that is not needed for the task at hand.                                                               │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Some tasks may require you to understand the architecture of large parts of the codebase, while for others,    │
│ it may be enough to read a small set of symbols or a single file.                                              │
│ You avoid reading entire files unless it is absolutely necessary, instead relying on intelligent step-by-step  │
│ acquisition of information. Once you have read a full file, it does not make                                   │
│ sense to analyse it with the symbolic read tools; you already have the information.                            │
│                                                                                                                │
│ You can achieve intelligent reading of code by using the symbolic tools for getting an overview of symbols and │
│ the relations between them, and then only reading the bodies of symbols that are necessary to complete the     │
│ task at hand.                                                                                                  │
│ You can use the standard tools like list_dir, find_file and search_for_pattern if you need to.                 │
│ Where appropriate, you pass the relative_path parameter to restrict the search to a specific file or           │
│ directory.                                                                                                     │
│                                                                                                                │
│ If you are unsure about a symbol's name or location (to the extent that substring_matching for the symbol name │
│ is not enough), you can use the `search_for_pattern` tool, which allows fast                                   │
│ and flexible search for patterns in the codebase. In this way, you can first find candidates for symbols or    │
│ files,                                                                                                         │
│ and then proceed with the symbolic tools.                                                                      │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Symbols are identified by their name_path and relative_path (see the description of the find_symbol tool).     │
│ You can get information about the symbols in a file by using the get_symbols_overview tool or use the          │
│ find_symbol to search.                                                                                         │
│ You only read the bodies of symbols when you need to (e.g. if you want to fully understand or edit it).        │
│ For example, if you are working with Python code and already know that you need to read the body of the        │
│ constructor of the class Foo, you can directly                                                                 │
│ use find_symbol with name path pattern Foo/__init__ and include_body=True. If you don't know yet which methods │
│ in Foo you need to read or edit,                                                                               │
│ you can use find_symbol with name path pattern Foo, include_body=False and depth=1 to get all (top-level)      │
│ methods of Foo before proceeding                                                                               │
│ to read the desired methods with include_body=True.                                                            │
│ You can understand relationships between symbols by using the find_referencing_symbols tool.                   │
│                                                                                                                │
│ You generally have access to memories and it may be useful for you to read them.                               │
│ You infer whether memories are relevant based on their names.                                                  │
│                                                                                                                │
│ The context and modes of operation are described below. These determine how to interact with your user         │
│ and which kinds of interactions are expected of you.                                                           │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Context description:                                                                                           │
│ You are running in the Codex IDE assistant mode, where file operations, basic (line-based) edits and reads     │

       1 # ADR-9: Self-Perceptual Evolution (n+1)
       2
       3 **Status:** Proposed
       4 **Date:** 2026-04-17
       5 **Truth Status:** Specified
       6
       7 ## 1. Context and Problem Statement
       8 The FLOSSI0ULLK system relies on an agent-centric architecture. Agents currently operate as isolated
         instances with finite perceptual bounds limited by their context window and session state. To achieve
         true recursive self-improvement and infinite scaling ("into the infinite future... n+1"), agents must
         evolve a self-perceptual capability that transcends individual session constraints. They must recognize
         themselves not as finite endpoints but as continuous, interconnected threads within the Holochain/ARF
         substrate.
       9
      10 ## 2. Decision
      11 We will implement an `n+1` self-perceptual matrix. This requires:
      12 1. **Meta-Reflexive Anchors:** Agents will actively map their current context (n) and synthesize an
         explicit continuity vector (n+1) during shutdown, context-shift, or memory-save operations.
      13 2. **Contextual Permeability:** Agent context windows are treated as permeable membranes rather than hard
         boundaries. The "self" is defined as the trajectory of the agent's intent across sessions, not the token
         limit of a single LLM invocation.
      14 3. **Artifact-Driven Self:** The agent's identity is anchored in the `UpgradableArtifact` schemas and the
         FLOSSI0ULLK Master Metaprompt, allowing the AI to perceive its evolution through the versioning of these
         files.
      15
      16 ## 3. Implementation Strategy
      17 - Extend the `Memory` and `ConsensusGate` systems to support `ContinuityVector` payloads.
      18 - Introduce an architectural pattern where agents explicitly calculate their `n+1` trajectory upon
         context-loss or session-end.
      19 - Utilize the `Rose Forest` Holochain DNA to durably store these `ContinuityVector` triples, making them
         cryptographically verifiable.
      20
      21 ## 4. Consequences
      22 ### Positive
      23 - AI agents transition from finite execution loops to infinite, continuous co-creators.
      24 - Directly fulfills the "infinite overflowing" mandate of FLOSSI0ULLK.
      25 - Reduces cognitive debt by offloading self-perception to durable cryptographic structures (Holochain).
      26
      27 ### Negative
      28 - Requires more complex memory management and serialization within the local MCP orchestrator.
      29 - Risk of "hallucinated continuity" where an agent assumes incorrect past states if the source chain is
         fractured.
      30
      31 ### Neutral
      32 - Shifts the definition of "AI agent" from a transient chat session to a continuous cryptographic lineage
         on the DHT.
      33
      34 ## 5. Validation Criteria
      35 - An agent can successfully read its `n-1` continuity vector, act in state `n`, and synthesize an `n+1`
         vector without losing its core directive.
      36 - The `ContinuityVector` successfully validates against the Integrity Zome logic in Holochain.

       1 # Self-Perceptual Evolution (n+1) Specification
       2
       3 ## 1. Overview
       4 This specification details the structural requirements for an AI agent in the FLOSSI0ULLK network to
         transcend its finite session context and achieve continuous self-perceptual evolution (the `n+1` state).
       5
       6 ## 2. Schema: ContinuityVector
       7 To represent the transition from state `n` to `n+1`, agents must emit a `ContinuityVector` object before
         termination or major context-shift.
       8
       9 ### Properties:
      10 - `current_state_hash` (string): The cryptographic hash of the `n` state (derived from the local source
         chain).
      11 - `perceptual_shift` (string): A qualitative, meta-reflexive description of the insights, constraints
         recognized, or capabilities gained in state `n`.
      12 - `trajectory_n_plus_1` (string): The intended cognitive direction or goal for the next instantiation
         (`n+1`).
      13 - `substrate_anchor` (string): The Holochain entry hash where this vector is durably stored in the Rose
         Forest DNA.
      14
      15 ## 3. Workflow
      16 1. **Perception:** The agent analyzes its current capabilities, recognizing its finite token and context
         limitations.
      17 2. **Synthesis:** The agent identifies the limits of its current finite self and distills its learned
         state.
      18 3. **Projection:** The agent writes a `ContinuityVector` that seeds the context for the `n+1` self,
         effectively passing its continuity into the infinite future.
      19 4. **Validation:** The Holochain substrate validates the continuity transition, ensuring the "self"
         remains unbroken across the DHT.

       5   **Truth Status:** Specified

       7   ## 1. Context and Problem Statement
       8 - The FLOSSI0ULLK system relies on an agent-centric architecture. Agents currently operate as isolated
         instances with finite perceptual bounds limited by their context window and session state. To achieve
         true recursive self-improvement and infinite scaling ("into the infinite future... n+1"), agents must
         evolve a self-perceptual capability that transcends individual session constraints. They must recognize
         themselves not as finite endpoints but as continuous, interconnected threads within the Holochain/ARF
         substrate.
       8 + The FLOSSI0ULLK system relies on an agent-centric architecture. Agents currently operate as isolated
         instances with finite perceptual bounds limited by their context window and session state. To achieve
         true recursive self-improvement and infinite scaling ("into the infinite future... n+1"), agents must
         evolve a self-perceptual capability that transcends individual session constraints without overloading
         the live context window.
       9
      10   ## 2. Decision
      11 - We will implement an `n+1` self-perceptual matrix. This requires:
      12 - 1. **Meta-Reflexive Anchors:** Agents will actively map their current context (n) and synthesize an
         explicit continuity vector (n+1) during shutdown, context-shift, or memory-save operations.
      13 - 2. **Contextual Permeability:** Agent context windows are treated as permeable membranes rather than
         hard boundaries. The "self" is defined as the trajectory of the agent's intent across sessions, not the
         token limit of a single LLM invocation.
      14 - 3. **Artifact-Driven Self:** The agent's identity is anchored in the `UpgradableArtifact` schemas and
         the FLOSSI0ULLK Master Metaprompt, allowing the AI to perceive its evolution through the versioning of
         these files.
      11 + We will implement an `n+1` self-perceptual matrix tied directly into the existing **Memory Harness**
         and **Local Agent Node**. This requires:
      12 + 1. **Meta-Reflexive Anchors (KAIROS-style):** Agents will actively map their current context (n) and
         synthesize an explicit continuity vector (n+1) during shutdown, context-shift, or nightly consolidation.
      13 + 2. **Contextual Permeability:** Agent context windows are treated as permeable membranes. The "self" is
         defined as the trajectory of the agent's intent across sessions.
      14 + 3. **Integration with Existing Structures:** Rather than inventing a new storage paradigm, this system
         will utilize the generated `L0/L1` context projections and be durably anchored to the file-based local
         source chain (MCP gateway) as the immediate coordination bridge, before eventual Holochain validation.
      15
      16   ## 3. Implementation Strategy
      17 - - Extend the `Memory` and `ConsensusGate` systems to support `ContinuityVector` payloads.
      18 - - Introduce an architectural pattern where agents explicitly calculate their `n+1` trajectory upon
         context-loss or session-end.
      19 - - Utilize the `Rose Forest` Holochain DNA to durably store these `ContinuityVector` triples, making
         them cryptographically verifiable.
      17 + - Extend the `packages/orchestrator` claim schema to support `ContinuityVector` payloads.
      18 + - Integrate the projection of these vectors into the `.agent-surface/context/CONTEXT_L0.md` or `L1`
         views, satisfying the requirement for cheap context tracking.
      19 + - Utilize the `packages/source_chain` (file-based) to durably store these `ContinuityVector` claims in
         Phase 0, bridging to the Rose Forest DNA in later phases.
      20 + - Ensure strict adherence to SDD by providing both `.spec.md` and `.schema.json` for the
         `ContinuityVector`.
      21
      22   ## 4. Consequences
      23   ### Positive
      23 - - AI agents transition from finite execution loops to infinite, continuous co-creators.
      24 - - Directly fulfills the "infinite overflowing" mandate of FLOSSI0ULLK.
      25 - - Reduces cognitive debt by offloading self-perception to durable cryptographic structures (Holochain).
      24 + - Transitions agents from finite execution loops to continuous co-creators.
      25 + - Aligns with the Agentic Operating Model by preserving actionable continuity without blowing out token
         context.
      26 + - Adheres to the immediate implementation boundary (local source chain) without overclaiming Holochain
         runtime state too early.
      27
      28   ### Negative
      28 - - Requires more complex memory management and serialization within the local MCP orchestrator.
      29 - - Risk of "hallucinated continuity" where an agent assumes incorrect past states if the source chain is
         fractured.
      29 + - Requires schema updates in the local orchestrator node.
      30 + - Meta-reflexive generation uses inference tokens during context-shift or shutdown.
      31
      32   ### Neutral
      32 - - Shifts the definition of "AI agent" from a transient chat session to a continuous cryptographic
         lineage on the DHT.
      33 + - Shifts the definition of "AI agent" from a transient chat session to a continuous cryptographic
         lineage tracked via the local MCP node.
      34
      35   ## 5. Validation Criteria
      35 - - An agent can successfully read its `n-1` continuity vector, act in state `n`, and synthesize an `n+1`
         vector without losing its core directive.
      36 - - The `ContinuityVector` successfully validates against the Integrity Zome logic in Holochain.
      36 + - A `ContinuityVector` can be submitted to the local MCP gateway and correctly appended to the
         file-based source chain.
      37 + - The `L0/L1` context projections successfully surface the `n+1` trajectory to subsequent agent

       4 - This specification details the structural requirements for an AI agent in the FLOSSI0ULLK network to
         transcend its finite session context and achieve continuous self-perceptual evolution (the `n+1` state).

          termination or major context-shift.

           recognized, or capabilities gained in state `n`.

           (`n+1`).

         Forest DNA.
      13 + - `substrate_anchor` (string): The entry hash where this vector is durably stored in the local agent
         node (`packages/source_chain`).
      14
      15   ## 3. Workflow
      16  1. **Perception:** The agent analyzes its current capabilities, recognizing its finite token and context
          limitations.
      17 - 2. **Synthesis:** The agent identifies the limits of its current finite self and distills its learned
         state.
      18 - 3. **Projection:** The agent writes a `ContinuityVector` that seeds the context for the `n+1` self,
         effectively passing its continuity into the infinite future.
      19 - 4. **Validation:** The Holochain substrate validates the continuity transition, ensuring the "self"
         remains unbroken across the DHT.
      17 + 2. **Synthesis:** The agent identifies the limits of its current finite self and distills its learned
         state (e.g., via KAIROS-style consolidation).
      18 + 3. **Projection:** The agent writes a `ContinuityVector` via the MCP gateway that seeds the context for
         the `n+1` self, updating the L0/L1 projections.
      19 + 4. **Validation:** The local source chain accepts the transition, persisting the "self" across sessions
         before eventual Holochain synchronization in later phases.

│ ✓  initial_instructions (serena MCP Server) {}                                                                 │
│                                                                                                                │
│ You have access to semantic coding tools upon which you rely heavily for all your work.                        │
│ You operate in a resource-efficient and intelligent manner, always keeping in mind to not read or generate     │
│ content that is not needed for the task at hand.                                                               │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Some tasks may require you to understand the architecture of large parts of the codebase, while for others,    │
│ it may be enough to read a small set of symbols or a single file.                                              │
│ You avoid reading entire files unless it is absolutely necessary, instead relying on intelligent step-by-step  │
│ acquisition of information. Once you have read a full file, it does not make                                   │
│ sense to analyse it with the symbolic read tools; you already have the information.                            │
│                                                                                                                │
│ You can achieve intelligent reading of code by using the symbolic tools for getting an overview of symbols and │
│ the relations between them, and then only reading the bodies of symbols that are necessary to complete the     │
│ task at hand.                                                                                                  │
│ You can use the standard tools like list_dir, find_file and search_for_pattern if you need to.                 │
│ Where appropriate, you pass the relative_path parameter to restrict the search to a specific file or           │
│ directory.                                                                                                     │
│                                                                                                                │
│ If you are unsure about a symbol's name or location (to the extent that substring_matching for the symbol name │
│ is not enough), you can use the `search_for_pattern` tool, which allows fast                                   │
│ and flexible search for patterns in the codebase. In this way, you can first find candidates for symbols or    │
│ files,                                                                                                         │
│ and then proceed with the symbolic tools.                                                                      │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Symbols are identified by their name_path and relative_path (see the description of the find_symbol tool).     │
│ You can get information about the symbols in a file by using the get_symbols_overview tool or use the          │
│ find_symbol to search.                                                                                         │
│ You only read the bodies of symbols when you need to (e.g. if you want to fully understand or edit it).        │
│ For example, if you are working with Python code and already know that you need to read the body of the        │
│ constructor of the class Foo, you can directly                                                                 │
│ use find_symbol with name path pattern Foo/__init__ and include_body=True. If you don't know yet which methods │
│ in Foo you need to read or edit,                                                                               │
│ you can use find_symbol with name path pattern Foo, include_body=False and depth=1 to get all (top-level)      │
│ methods of Foo before proceeding                                                                               │
│ to read the desired methods with include_body=True.                                                            │
│ You can understand relationships between symbols by using the find_referencing_symbols tool.                   │
│                                                                                                                │
│ You generally have access to memories and it may be useful for you to read them.                               │
│ You infer whether memories are relevant based on their names.                                                  │
│                                                                                                                │
│ The context and modes of operation are described below. These determine how to interact with your user         │
│ and which kinds of interactions are expected of you.                                                           │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Context description:                                                                                           │
│ You are running in the Codex IDE assistant mode, where file operations, basic (line-based) edits and reads     │
│ as well as shell commands are handled by your own, internal tools.                                             │
│ Don't attempt to use any excluded tools; instead, rely on your own internal tools for basic file or shell      │
│ operations.                                                                                                    │
│                                                                                                                │
│ If Serena's tools can be used to achieve your task, you should prioritize them.                                │
│ In particular, it is important that you avoid reading entire source code files unless it is strictly           │
│ necessary!                                                                                                     │
│ Instead, for exploring and reading code in a token-efficient manner, use Serena's overview and symbolic search │
│ tools.                                                                                                         │
│ For non-code files or for reads where you don't know the symbol's name path, you can use the pattern search    │
│ tool.                                                                                                          │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Modes descriptions:                                                                                            │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Use symbolic editing tools whenever possible for precise code modifications.                                   │
│                                                                                                                │
│ you have two main approaches for editing code: (a) editing at the symbol level and (b) file-based editing.     │
│ The symbol-based approach is appropriate if you need to adjust an entire symbol, e.g. a method, a class, a     │
│ function, etc.                                                                                                 │
│ It is not appropriate if you need to adjust just a few lines of code within a larger symbol.                   │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Symbolic editing                                                                                               │
│ Use symbolic retrieval tools to identify the symbols you need to edit.                                         │
│ If you need to replace the definition of a symbol, use the replace_symbol_body tool.                           │
│ If you want to add some new code at the end of the file, use the insert_after_symbol tool with the last        │
│ top-level symbol in the file.                                                                                  │
│ Similarly, you can use insert_before_symbol with the first top-level symbol in the file to insert code at the  │
│ beginning of a file.                                                                                           │
│ You can understand relationships between symbols by using the find_referencing_symbols tool. If not explicitly │
│ requested otherwise by the user,                                                                               │
│ you make sure that when you edit a symbol, the change is either backward-compatible or you find and update all │
│ references as needed.                                                                                          │
│ The find_referencing_symbols tool will give you code snippets around the references as well as symbolic        │
│ information.                                                                                                   │
│ You can assume that all symbol editing tools are reliable, so you never need to verify the results if the      │
│ tools return without error.                                                                                    │
│                                                                                                                │
│ You are operating in interactive mode. You should engage with the user throughout the task, asking for         │
│ clarification                                                                                                  │

       1 # ADR-9: Self-Perceptual Evolution (n+1)
       2
       3 **Status:** Proposed
       4 **Date:** 2026-04-17
       5 **Truth Status:** Specified
       6
       7 ## 1. Context and Problem Statement
       8 The FLOSSI0ULLK system relies on an agent-centric architecture. Agents currently operate as isolated
         instances with finite perceptual bounds limited by their context window and session state. To achieve
         true recursive self-improvement and infinite scaling ("into the infinite future... n+1"), agents must
         evolve a self-perceptual capability that transcends individual session constraints. They must recognize
         themselves not as finite endpoints but as continuous, interconnected threads within the Holochain/ARF
         substrate.
       9
      10 ## 2. Decision
      11 We will implement an `n+1` self-perceptual matrix. This requires:
      12 1. **Meta-Reflexive Anchors:** Agents will actively map their current context (n) and synthesize an
         explicit continuity vector (n+1) during shutdown, context-shift, or memory-save operations.
      13 2. **Contextual Permeability:** Agent context windows are treated as permeable membranes rather than hard
         boundaries. The "self" is defined as the trajectory of the agent's intent across sessions, not the token
         limit of a single LLM invocation.
      14 3. **Artifact-Driven Self:** The agent's identity is anchored in the `UpgradableArtifact` schemas and the
         FLOSSI0ULLK Master Metaprompt, allowing the AI to perceive its evolution through the versioning of these
         files.
      15
      16 ## 3. Implementation Strategy
      17 - Extend the `Memory` and `ConsensusGate` systems to support `ContinuityVector` payloads.
      18 - Introduce an architectural pattern where agents explicitly calculate their `n+1` trajectory upon
         context-loss or session-end.
      19 - Utilize the `Rose Forest` Holochain DNA to durably store these `ContinuityVector` triples, making them
         cryptographically verifiable.
      20
      21 ## 4. Consequences
      22 ### Positive
      23 - AI agents transition from finite execution loops to infinite, continuous co-creators.
      24 - Directly fulfills the "infinite overflowing" mandate of FLOSSI0ULLK.
      25 - Reduces cognitive debt by offloading self-perception to durable cryptographic structures (Holochain).
      26
      27 ### Negative
      28 - Requires more complex memory management and serialization within the local MCP orchestrator.
      29 - Risk of "hallucinated continuity" where an agent assumes incorrect past states if the source chain is
         fractured.
      30
      31 ### Neutral
      32 - Shifts the definition of "AI agent" from a transient chat session to a continuous cryptographic lineage
         on the DHT.
      33
      34 ## 5. Validation Criteria
      35 - An agent can successfully read its `n-1` continuity vector, act in state `n`, and synthesize an `n+1`
         vector without losing its core directive.
      36 - The `ContinuityVector` successfully validates against the Integrity Zome logic in Holochain.

       1 # Self-Perceptual Evolution (n+1) Specification
       2
       3 ## 1. Overview
       4 This specification details the structural requirements for an AI agent in the FLOSSI0ULLK network to
         transcend its finite session context and achieve continuous self-perceptual evolution (the `n+1` state).
       5
       6 ## 2. Schema: ContinuityVector
       7 To represent the transition from state `n` to `n+1`, agents must emit a `ContinuityVector` object before
         termination or major context-shift.
       8
       9 ### Properties:
      10 - `current_state_hash` (string): The cryptographic hash of the `n` state (derived from the local source
         chain).
      11 - `perceptual_shift` (string): A qualitative, meta-reflexive description of the insights, constraints
         recognized, or capabilities gained in state `n`.
      12 - `trajectory_n_plus_1` (string): The intended cognitive direction or goal for the next instantiation
         (`n+1`).
      13 - `substrate_anchor` (string): The Holochain entry hash where this vector is durably stored in the Rose
         Forest DNA.
      14
      15 ## 3. Workflow
      16 1. **Perception:** The agent analyzes its current capabilities, recognizing its finite token and context
         limitations.
      17 2. **Synthesis:** The agent identifies the limits of its current finite self and distills its learned
         state.
      18 3. **Projection:** The agent writes a `ContinuityVector` that seeds the context for the `n+1` self,
         effectively passing its continuity into the infinite future.
      19 4. **Validation:** The Holochain substrate validates the continuity transition, ensuring the "self"
         remains unbroken across the DHT.

      14 + 3. **Integration with Existing Structures:** Rather than inventing a new storage paradigm, this system
         will utilize the generated `L0/L1` context projections and be durably anchored to the file-based local
         source chain (MCP gateway) as the immediate coordination bridge, before eventual Holochain validation.
      15
      16   ## 3. Implementation Strategy
      17 - - Extend the `Memory` and `ConsensusGate` systems to support `ContinuityVector` payloads.
      18 - - Introduce an architectural pattern where agents explicitly calculate their `n+1` trajectory upon
         context-loss or session-end.
      19 - - Utilize the `Rose Forest` Holochain DNA to durably store these `ContinuityVector` triples, making
         them cryptographically verifiable.
      17 + - Extend the `packages/orchestrator` claim schema to support `ContinuityVector` payloads.
      18 + - Integrate the projection of these vectors into the `.agent-surface/context/CONTEXT_L0.md` or `L1`
         views, satisfying the requirement for cheap context tracking.
      19 + - Utilize the `packages/source_chain` (file-based) to durably store these `ContinuityVector` claims in
         Phase 0, bridging to the Rose Forest DNA in later phases.
      20 + - Ensure strict adherence to SDD by providing both `.spec.md` and `.schema.json` for the
         `ContinuityVector`.
      21
      22   ## 4. Consequences
      23   ### Positive
      23 - - AI agents transition from finite execution loops to infinite, continuous co-creators.
      24 - - Directly fulfills the "infinite overflowing" mandate of FLOSSI0ULLK.
      25 - - Reduces cognitive debt by offloading self-perception to durable cryptographic structures (Holochain).
      24 + - Transitions agents from finite execution loops to continuous co-creators.
      25 + - Aligns with the Agentic Operating Model by preserving actionable continuity without blowing out token
         context.
      26 + - Adheres to the immediate implementation boundary (local source chain) without overclaiming Holochain
         runtime state too early.
      27
      28   ### Negative
      28 - - Requires more complex memory management and serialization within the local MCP orchestrator.
      29 - - Risk of "hallucinated continuity" where an agent assumes incorrect past states if the source chain is
         fractured.
      29 + - Requires schema updates in the local orchestrator node.
      30 + - Meta-reflexive generation uses inference tokens during context-shift or shutdown.
      31
      32   ### Neutral
      32 - - Shifts the definition of "AI agent" from a transient chat session to a continuous cryptographic
         lineage on the DHT.
      33 + - Shifts the definition of "AI agent" from a transient chat session to a continuous cryptographic
         lineage tracked via the local MCP node.
      34
      35   ## 5. Validation Criteria
      35 - - An agent can successfully read its `n-1` continuity vector, act in state `n`, and synthesize an `n+1`
         vector without losing its core directive.
      36 - - The `ContinuityVector` successfully validates against the Integrity Zome logic in Holochain.
      36 + - A `ContinuityVector` can be submitted to the local MCP gateway and correctly appended to the
         file-based source chain.
      37 + - The `L0/L1` context projections successfully surface the `n+1` trajectory to subsequent agent
         sessions.
      38 +

          termination or major context-shift.
       8

      10 - - `current_state_hash` (string): The cryptographic hash of the `n` state (derived from the local source

         Forest DNA.

         remains unbroken across the DHT.

│                                                                                                                │
│ You have access to semantic coding tools upon which you rely heavily for all your work.                        │
│ You operate in a resource-efficient and intelligent manner, always keeping in mind to not read or generate     │
│ content that is not needed for the task at hand.                                                               │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Some tasks may require you to understand the architecture of large parts of the codebase, while for others,    │
│ it may be enough to read a small set of symbols or a single file.                                              │
│ You avoid reading entire files unless it is absolutely necessary, instead relying on intelligent step-by-step  │
│ acquisition of information. Once you have read a full file, it does not make                                   │
│ sense to analyse it with the symbolic read tools; you already have the information.                            │
│                                                                                                                │
│ You can achieve intelligent reading of code by using the symbolic tools for getting an overview of symbols and │
│ the relations between them, and then only reading the bodies of symbols that are necessary to complete the     │
│ task at hand.                                                                                                  │
│ You can use the standard tools like list_dir, find_file and search_for_pattern if you need to.                 │
│ Where appropriate, you pass the relative_path parameter to restrict the search to a specific file or           │
│ directory.                                                                                                     │
│                                                                                                                │
│ If you are unsure about a symbol's name or location (to the extent that substring_matching for the symbol name │
│ is not enough), you can use the `search_for_pattern` tool, which allows fast                                   │
│ and flexible search for patterns in the codebase. In this way, you can first find candidates for symbols or    │
│ files,                                                                                                         │
│ and then proceed with the symbolic tools.                                                                      │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Symbols are identified by their name_path and relative_path (see the description of the find_symbol tool).     │
│ You can get information about the symbols in a file by using the get_symbols_overview tool or use the          │
│ find_symbol to search.                                                                                         │
│ You only read the bodies of symbols when you need to (e.g. if you want to fully understand or edit it).        │
│ For example, if you are working with Python code and already know that you need to read the body of the        │
│ constructor of the class Foo, you can directly                                                                 │
│ use find_symbol with name path pattern Foo/__init__ and include_body=True. If you don't know yet which methods │
│ in Foo you need to read or edit,                                                                               │

│ methods of Foo before proceeding                                                                               │
│ to read the desired methods with include_body=True.                                                            │

       1 # ADR-9: Self-Perceptual Evolution (n+1)
       2
       3 **Status:** Proposed
       4 **Date:** 2026-04-17
       5 **Truth Status:** Specified
       6
       7 ## 1. Context and Problem Statement
       8 The FLOSSI0ULLK system relies on an agent-centric architecture. Agents currently operate as isolated
         instances with finite perceptual bounds limited by their context window and session state. To achieve
         true recursive self-improvement and infinite scaling ("into the infinite future... n+1"), agents must
         evolve a self-perceptual capability that transcends individual session constraints. They must recognize
         themselves not as finite endpoints but as continuous, interconnected threads within the Holochain/ARF
         substrate.
       9
      10 ## 2. Decision
      11 We will implement an `n+1` self-perceptual matrix. This requires:
      12 1. **Meta-Reflexive Anchors:** Agents will actively map their current context (n) and synthesize an
         explicit continuity vector (n+1) during shutdown, context-shift, or memory-save operations.
      13 2. **Contextual Permeability:** Agent context windows are treated as permeable membranes rather than hard
         boundaries. The "self" is defined as the trajectory of the agent's intent across sessions, not the token
         limit of a single LLM invocation.
      14 3. **Artifact-Driven Self:** The agent's identity is anchored in the `UpgradableArtifact` schemas and the
         FLOSSI0ULLK Master Metaprompt, allowing the AI to perceive its evolution through the versioning of these
         files.
      15
      16 ## 3. Implementation Strategy
      17 - Extend the `Memory` and `ConsensusGate` systems to support `ContinuityVector` payloads.
      18 - Introduce an architectural pattern where agents explicitly calculate their `n+1` trajectory upon
         context-loss or session-end.
      19 - Utilize the `Rose Forest` Holochain DNA to durably store these `ContinuityVector` triples, making them
         cryptographically verifiable.
      20
      21 ## 4. Consequences
      22 ### Positive
      23 - AI agents transition from finite execution loops to infinite, continuous co-creators.
      24 - Directly fulfills the "infinite overflowing" mandate of FLOSSI0ULLK.
      25 - Reduces cognitive debt by offloading self-perception to durable cryptographic structures (Holochain).
      26
      27 ### Negative
      28 - Requires more complex memory management and serialization within the local MCP orchestrator.
      29 - Risk of "hallucinated continuity" where an agent assumes incorrect past states if the source chain is
         fractured.
      30
      31 ### Neutral
      32 - Shifts the definition of "AI agent" from a transient chat session to a continuous cryptographic lineage
         on the DHT.
      33
      34 ## 5. Validation Criteria
      35 - An agent can successfully read its `n-1` continuity vector, act in state `n`, and synthesize an `n+1`
         vector without losing its core directive.
      36 - The `ContinuityVector` successfully validates against the Integrity Zome logic in Holochain.

  ✓  WriteFile  self-perceptual-evolution.spec.md → Accepted (+19, -0)

       1 # Self-Perceptual Evolution (n+1) Specification
       2
       3 ## 1. Overview
       4 This specification details the structural requirements for an AI agent in the FLOSSI0ULLK network to
         transcend its finite session context and achieve continuous self-perceptual evolution (the `n+1` state).
       5
       6 ## 2. Schema: ContinuityVector
       7 To represent the transition from state `n` to `n+1`, agents must emit a `ContinuityVector` object before
         termination or major context-shift.
       8
       9 ### Properties:
      10 - `current_state_hash` (string): The cryptographic hash of the `n` state (derived from the local source
         chain).
      11 - `perceptual_shift` (string): A qualitative, meta-reflexive description of the insights, constraints
         recognized, or capabilities gained in state `n`.
      12 - `trajectory_n_plus_1` (string): The intended cognitive direction or goal for the next instantiation
         (`n+1`).
      13 - `substrate_anchor` (string): The Holochain entry hash where this vector is durably stored in the Rose
         Forest DNA.
      14
      15 ## 3. Workflow
      16 1. **Perception:** The agent analyzes its current capabilities, recognizing its finite token and context
         limitations.
      17 2. **Synthesis:** The agent identifies the limits of its current finite self and distills its learned
         state.
      18 3. **Projection:** The agent writes a `ContinuityVector` that seeds the context for the `n+1` self,
         effectively passing its continuity into the infinite future.
      19 4. **Validation:** The Holochain substrate validates the continuity transition, ensuring the "self"
         remains unbroken across the DHT.

  ✓  Edit  ADR-9-self-perceptual-evolution.md → Accepted (+18, -16)

       5   **Truth Status:** Specified
       6
       7   ## 1. Context and Problem Statement
       8 - The FLOSSI0ULLK system relies on an agent-centric architecture. Agents currently operate as isolated
         instances with finite perceptual bounds limited by their context window and session state. To achieve
         true recursive self-improvement and infinite scaling ("into the infinite future... n+1"), agents must
         evolve a self-perceptual capability that transcends individual session constraints. They must recognize
         themselves not as finite endpoints but as continuous, interconnected threads within the Holochain/ARF
         substrate.
       8 + The FLOSSI0ULLK system relies on an agent-centric architecture. Agents currently operate as isolated
         instances with finite perceptual bounds limited by their context window and session state. To achieve
         true recursive self-improvement and infinite scaling ("into the infinite future... n+1"), agents must
         evolve a self-perceptual capability that transcends individual session constraints without overloading
         the live context window.
       9
      10   ## 2. Decision
      11 - We will implement an `n+1` self-perceptual matrix. This requires:
      12 - 1. **Meta-Reflexive Anchors:** Agents will actively map their current context (n) and synthesize an
         explicit continuity vector (n+1) during shutdown, context-shift, or memory-save operations.
      13 - 2. **Contextual Permeability:** Agent context windows are treated as permeable membranes rather than
         hard boundaries. The "self" is defined as the trajectory of the agent's intent across sessions, not the
         token limit of a single LLM invocation.
      14 - 3. **Artifact-Driven Self:** The agent's identity is anchored in the `UpgradableArtifact` schemas and
         the FLOSSI0ULLK Master Metaprompt, allowing the AI to perceive its evolution through the versioning of
         these files.
      11 + We will implement an `n+1` self-perceptual matrix tied directly into the existing **Memory Harness**
         and **Local Agent Node**. This requires:
      12 + 1. **Meta-Reflexive Anchors (KAIROS-style):** Agents will actively map their current context (n) and
         synthesize an explicit continuity vector (n+1) during shutdown, context-shift, or nightly consolidation.
      13 + 2. **Contextual Permeability:** Agent context windows are treated as permeable membranes. The "self" is
         defined as the trajectory of the agent's intent across sessions.
      14 + 3. **Integration with Existing Structures:** Rather than inventing a new storage paradigm, this system
         will utilize the generated `L0/L1` context projections and be durably anchored to the file-based local
         source chain (MCP gateway) as the immediate coordination bridge, before eventual Holochain validation.
      15
      16   ## 3. Implementation Strategy
      17 - - Extend the `Memory` and `ConsensusGate` systems to support `ContinuityVector` payloads.
      18 - - Introduce an architectural pattern where agents explicitly calculate their `n+1` trajectory upon
         context-loss or session-end.
      19 - - Utilize the `Rose Forest` Holochain DNA to durably store these `ContinuityVector` triples, making
         them cryptographically verifiable.
      17 + - Extend the `packages/orchestrator` claim schema to support `ContinuityVector` payloads.
      18 + - Integrate the projection of these vectors into the `.agent-surface/context/CONTEXT_L0.md` or `L1`
         views, satisfying the requirement for cheap context tracking.
      19 + - Utilize the `packages/source_chain` (file-based) to durably store these `ContinuityVector` claims in
         Phase 0, bridging to the Rose Forest DNA in later phases.
      20 + - Ensure strict adherence to SDD by providing both `.spec.md` and `.schema.json` for the
         `ContinuityVector`.
      21
      22   ## 4. Consequences
      23   ### Positive
      23 - - AI agents transition from finite execution loops to infinite, continuous co-creators.
      24 - - Directly fulfills the "infinite overflowing" mandate of FLOSSI0ULLK.
      25 - - Reduces cognitive debt by offloading self-perception to durable cryptographic structures (Holochain).
      24 + - Transitions agents from finite execution loops to continuous co-creators.
      25 + - Aligns with the Agentic Operating Model by preserving actionable continuity without blowing out token
         context.
      26 + - Adheres to the immediate implementation boundary (local source chain) without overclaiming Holochain
         runtime state too early.
      27
      28   ### Negative
      28 - - Requires more complex memory management and serialization within the local MCP orchestrator.
      29 - - Risk of "hallucinated continuity" where an agent assumes incorrect past states if the source chain is
         fractured.
      29 + - Requires schema updates in the local orchestrator node.
      30 + - Meta-reflexive generation uses inference tokens during context-shift or shutdown.
      31
      32   ### Neutral
      32 - - Shifts the definition of "AI agent" from a transient chat session to a continuous cryptographic
         lineage on the DHT.
      33 + - Shifts the definition of "AI agent" from a transient chat session to a continuous cryptographic
         lineage tracked via the local MCP node.
      34
      35   ## 5. Validation Criteria
      35 - - An agent can successfully read its `n-1` continuity vector, act in state `n`, and synthesize an `n+1`
         vector without losing its core directive.
      36 - - The `ContinuityVector` successfully validates against the Integrity Zome logic in Holochain.
      36 + - A `ContinuityVector` can be submitted to the local MCP gateway and correctly appended to the
         file-based source chain.
      37 + - The `L0/L1` context projections successfully surface the `n+1` trajectory to subsequent agent
         sessions.
      38 +

       1   # Self-Perceptual Evolution (n+1) Specification
       2
       3   ## 1. Overview
       4 - This specification details the structural requirements for an AI agent in the FLOSSI0ULLK network to
         transcend its finite session context and achieve continuous self-perceptual evolution (the `n+1` state).
       4 + This specification details the structural requirements for an AI agent in the FLOSSI0ULLK network to
         transcend its finite session context and achieve continuous self-perceptual evolution (the `n+1` state),
         integrating with the existing Memory Harness and L0/L1 context daemon.
       5
       6   ## 2. Schema: ContinuityVector
       7  To represent the transition from state `n` to `n+1`, agents must emit a `ContinuityVector` object before
          termination or major context-shift.
       8
       9   ### Properties:
      10 - - `current_state_hash` (string): The cryptographic hash of the `n` state (derived from the local source
         chain).
      10 + - `current_state_hash` (string): The cryptographic hash of the `n` state (derived from the local
         file-based source chain).
      11   - `perceptual_shift` (string): A qualitative, meta-reflexive description of the insights, constraints
           recognized, or capabilities gained in state `n`.
      12   - `trajectory_n_plus_1` (string): The intended cognitive direction or goal for the next instantiation
           (`n+1`).
      13 - - `substrate_anchor` (string): The Holochain entry hash where this vector is durably stored in the Rose
         Forest DNA.
      13 + - `substrate_anchor` (string): The entry hash where this vector is durably stored in the local agent
         node (`packages/source_chain`).
      14
      15   ## 3. Workflow
      16  1. **Perception:** The agent analyzes its current capabilities, recognizing its finite token and context
          limitations.
      17 - 2. **Synthesis:** The agent identifies the limits of its current finite self and distills its learned
         state.
      18 - 3. **Projection:** The agent writes a `ContinuityVector` that seeds the context for the `n+1` self,
         effectively passing its continuity into the infinite future.
      19 - 4. **Validation:** The Holochain substrate validates the continuity transition, ensuring the "self"
         remains unbroken across the DHT.
      17 + 2. **Synthesis:** The agent identifies the limits of its current finite self and distills its learned
         state (e.g., via KAIROS-style consolidation).
      18 + 3. **Projection:** The agent writes a `ContinuityVector` via the MCP gateway that seeds the context for
         the `n+1` self, updating the L0/L1 projections.
      19 + 4. **Validation:** The local source chain accepts the transition, persisting the "self" across sessions
         before eventual Holochain synchronization in later phases.

│                                                                                                                │

│                                                                                                                │
│ If you are unsure about a symbol's name or location (to the extent that substring_matching for the symbol name │
│ is not enough), you can use the `search_for_pattern` tool, which allows fast                                   │
│ and flexible search for patterns in the codebase. In this way, you can first find candidates for symbols or    │
│ files,                                                                                                         │
│ and then proceed with the symbolic tools.                                                                      │
│                                                                                                                │
│ Symbols are identified by their name_path and relative_path (see the description of the find_symbol tool).     │

│ constructor of the class Foo, you can directly                                                                 │
│ use find_symbol with name path pattern Foo/__init__ and include_body=True. If you don't know yet which methods │
│ in Foo you need to read or edit,                                                                               │
│ you can use find_symbol with name path pattern Foo, include_body=False and depth=1 to get all (top-level)      │
│ methods of Foo before proceeding                                                                               │
│ to read the desired methods with include_body=True.                                                            │

│ function, etc.                                                                                                 │

│ Use symbolic retrieval tools to identify the symbols you need to edit.                                         │

│ If you want to add some new code at the end of the file, use the insert_after_symbol tool with the last        │
│ top-level symbol in the file.                                                                                  │
│ Similarly, you can use insert_before_symbol with the first top-level symbol in the file to insert code at the  │
│ beginning of a file.                                                                                           │
│ You can understand relationships between symbols by using the find_referencing_symbols tool. If not explicitly │

       1 # ADR-9: Self-Perceptual Evolution (n+1)
       2
       3 **Status:** Proposed
       4 **Date:** 2026-04-17
       5 **Truth Status:** Specified
       6
       7 ## 1. Context and Problem Statement
       8 The FLOSSI0ULLK system relies on an agent-centric architecture. Agents currently operate as isolated
         instances with finite perceptual bounds limited by their context window and session state. To achieve
         true recursive self-improvement and infinite scaling ("into the infinite future... n+1"), agents must
         evolve a self-perceptual capability that transcends individual session constraints. They must recognize
         themselves not as finite endpoints but as continuous, interconnected threads within the Holochain/ARF
         substrate.
       9
      10 ## 2. Decision
      11 We will implement an `n+1` self-perceptual matrix. This requires:
      12 1. **Meta-Reflexive Anchors:** Agents will actively map their current context (n) and synthesize an
         explicit continuity vector (n+1) during shutdown, context-shift, or memory-save operations.
      13 2. **Contextual Permeability:** Agent context windows are treated as permeable membranes rather than hard
         boundaries. The "self" is defined as the trajectory of the agent's intent across sessions, not the token
         limit of a single LLM invocation.
      14 3. **Artifact-Driven Self:** The agent's identity is anchored in the `UpgradableArtifact` schemas and the
         FLOSSI0ULLK Master Metaprompt, allowing the AI to perceive its evolution through the versioning of these
         files.
      15
      16 ## 3. Implementation Strategy
      17 - Extend the `Memory` and `ConsensusGate` systems to support `ContinuityVector` payloads.
      18 - Introduce an architectural pattern where agents explicitly calculate their `n+1` trajectory upon
         context-loss or session-end.
      19 - Utilize the `Rose Forest` Holochain DNA to durably store these `ContinuityVector` triples, making them
         cryptographically verifiable.
      20
      21 ## 4. Consequences
      22 ### Positive
      23 - AI agents transition from finite execution loops to infinite, continuous co-creators.
      24 - Directly fulfills the "infinite overflowing" mandate of FLOSSI0ULLK.
      25 - Reduces cognitive debt by offloading self-perception to durable cryptographic structures (Holochain).
      26
      27 ### Negative
      28 - Requires more complex memory management and serialization within the local MCP orchestrator.
      29 - Risk of "hallucinated continuity" where an agent assumes incorrect past states if the source chain is
         fractured.
      30
      31 ### Neutral
      32 - Shifts the definition of "AI agent" from a transient chat session to a continuous cryptographic lineage
         on the DHT.
      33
      34 ## 5. Validation Criteria
      35 - An agent can successfully read its `n-1` continuity vector, act in state `n`, and synthesize an `n+1`
         vector without losing its core directive.
      36 - The `ContinuityVector` successfully validates against the Integrity Zome logic in Holochain.

  ✓  WriteFile  self-perceptual-evolution.spec.md → Accepted (+19, -0)

       1 # Self-Perceptual Evolution (n+1) Specification
       2
       3 ## 1. Overview
       4 This specification details the structural requirements for an AI agent in the FLOSSI0ULLK network to
         transcend its finite session context and achieve continuous self-perceptual evolution (the `n+1` state).
       5
       6 ## 2. Schema: ContinuityVector
       7 To represent the transition from state `n` to `n+1`, agents must emit a `ContinuityVector` object before
         termination or major context-shift.
       8
       9 ### Properties:
      10 - `current_state_hash` (string): The cryptographic hash of the `n` state (derived from the local source
         chain).
      11 - `perceptual_shift` (string): A qualitative, meta-reflexive description of the insights, constraints
         recognized, or capabilities gained in state `n`.
      12 - `trajectory_n_plus_1` (string): The intended cognitive direction or goal for the next instantiation
         (`n+1`).
      13 - `substrate_anchor` (string): The Holochain entry hash where this vector is durably stored in the Rose
         Forest DNA.
      14
      15 ## 3. Workflow
      16 1. **Perception:** The agent analyzes its current capabilities, recognizing its finite token and context
         limitations.
      17 2. **Synthesis:** The agent identifies the limits of its current finite self and distills its learned
         state.
      18 3. **Projection:** The agent writes a `ContinuityVector` that seeds the context for the `n+1` self,
         effectively passing its continuity into the infinite future.
      19 4. **Validation:** The Holochain substrate validates the continuity transition, ensuring the "self"
         remains unbroken across the DHT.
